class \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1DenseTimeSparseProduct}{Dense\+Time\+Sparse\+Product}}

class \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1DGMRES}{DGMRES}}
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em A Restarted \doxylink{classEigen_1_1GMRES}{GMRES} with deflation. This class implements a modification of the \doxylink{classEigen_1_1GMRES}{GMRES} solver for sparse linear systems. The basis is built with modified Gram-\/\+Schmidt. At each restart, a few approximated eigenvectors corresponding to the smallest eigenvalues are used to build a preconditioner for the next cycle. This preconditioner for deflation can be combined with any other preconditioner, the \doxylink{classEigen_1_1IncompleteLUT}{Incomplete\+LUT} for instance. The preconditioner is applied at right of the matrix and the combination is multiplicative. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item

The Index type as used for the API. 

To change this, {\ttfamily \#define} the preprocessor symbol {\ttfamily EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEFAULT\+\_\+\+DENSE\+\_\+\+INDEX\+\_\+\+TYPE}. \begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\textbackslash{}blank Topic\+Preprocessor\+Directives, Storage\+Index. 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\Hypertarget{namespaceEigen_ae614aa7cdd687fb5c421a54f2ce5c361}\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!EulerAxis@{EulerAxis}}
\index{EulerAxis@{EulerAxis}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{EulerAxis}{EulerAxis}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespaceEigen_ae614aa7cdd687fb5c421a54f2ce5c361} 
enum \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceEigen_ae614aa7cdd687fb5c421a54f2ce5c361}{Eigen\+::\+Euler\+Axis}}}



Representation of a fixed signed rotation axis for \doxylink{classEigen_1_1EulerSystem}{Euler\+System}. 

Values here represent\+:
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item The axis of the rotation\+: X, Y or Z.
\item The sign (i.\+e. direction of the rotation along the axis)\+: positive(+) or negative(-\/)
\end{DoxyItemize}

Therefore, this could express all the axes \{+X,+Y,+Z,-\/X,-\/Y,-\/Z\}

For positive axis, use +EULER\+\_\+\{axis\}, and for negative axis use -\/EULER\+\_\+\{axis\}. \begin{DoxyEnumFields}[2]{Enumerator}
\raisebox{\heightof{T}}[0pt][0pt]{\index{EULER\_X@{EULER\_X}!Eigen@{Eigen}}\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!EULER\_X@{EULER\_X}}}\Hypertarget{namespaceEigen_ae614aa7cdd687fb5c421a54f2ce5c361ae8110af93d433bfcf247d6bac5e1d387}\label{namespaceEigen_ae614aa7cdd687fb5c421a54f2ce5c361} 
EULER\+\_\+X&the X axis \\
\hline

\raisebox{\heightof{T}}[0pt][0pt]{\index{EULER\_Y@{EULER\_Y}!Eigen@{Eigen}}\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!EULER\_Y@{EULER\_Y}}}\Hypertarget{namespaceEigen_ae614aa7cdd687fb5c421a54f2ce5c361a7309edb53a9d9cdb77fac7c1e9200263}\label{namespaceEigen_ae614aa7cdd687fb5c421a54f2ce5c361} 
EULER\+\_\+Y&the Y axis \\
\hline

\raisebox{\heightof{T}}[0pt][0pt]{\index{EULER\_Z@{EULER\_Z}!Eigen@{Eigen}}\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!EULER\_Z@{EULER\_Z}}}\Hypertarget{namespaceEigen_ae614aa7cdd687fb5c421a54f2ce5c361a0c641fd5050b5219d6c172ac83fb379d}\label{namespaceEigen_ae614aa7cdd687fb5c421a54f2ce5c361} 
EULER\+\_\+Z&the Z axis \\

\Hypertarget{namespaceEigen_ae614aa7cdd687fb5c421a54f2ce5c361}\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!EulerAxis@{EulerAxis}}
\index{EulerAxis@{EulerAxis}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{EulerAxis}{EulerAxis}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [2/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespaceEigen_ae614aa7cdd687fb5c421a54f2ce5c361} 
enum \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceEigen_ae614aa7cdd687fb5c421a54f2ce5c361}{Eigen\+::\+Euler\+Axis}}}



Representation of a fixed signed rotation axis for \doxylink{classEigen_1_1EulerSystem}{Euler\+System}. 

Values here represent\+:
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item The axis of the rotation\+: X, Y or Z.
\item The sign (i.\+e. direction of the rotation along the axis)\+: positive(+) or negative(-\/)
\end{DoxyItemize}

Therefore, this could express all the axes \{+X,+Y,+Z,-\/X,-\/Y,-\/Z\}

For positive axis, use +EULER\+\_\+\{axis\}, and for negative axis use -\/EULER\+\_\+\{axis\}. \begin{DoxyEnumFields}[2]{Enumerator}
\raisebox{\heightof{T}}[0pt][0pt]{\index{EULER\_X@{EULER\_X}!Eigen@{Eigen}}\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!EULER\_X@{EULER\_X}}}\Hypertarget{namespaceEigen_ae614aa7cdd687fb5c421a54f2ce5c361ae8110af93d433bfcf247d6bac5e1d387}\label{namespaceEigen_ae614aa7cdd687fb5c421a54f2ce5c361}

\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_af2b60117c00a6e75812de43bfe7db3b1}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+STRONG\+\_\+\+INLINE}} const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1CwiseTernaryOp}{Eigen\+::\+Cwise\+Ternary\+Op}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structEigen_1_1internal_1_1scalar__betainc__op}{Eigen\+::internal\+::scalar\+\_\+betainc\+\_\+op}}$<$ typename Arg\+XDerived\+::\+Scalar $>$, const Arg\+ADerived, const Arg\+BDerived, const Arg\+XDerived $>$ Eigen\+::betainc (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase}{Eigen\+::\+Array\+Base}}$<$ Arg\+ADerived $>$ \&}]{a}{, }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase}{Eigen\+::\+Array\+Base}}$<$ Arg\+BDerived $>$ \&}]{b}{, }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase}{Eigen\+::\+Array\+Base}}$<$ Arg\+XDerived $>$ \&}]{x}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\textbackslash{}cpp11 \begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of the coefficient-\/wise betainc({\itshape x}, {\itshape a}, {\itshape b}) to the given arrays.
\end{DoxyReturn}
This function computes the regularized incomplete beta function (integral).

\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
This function supports only float and double scalar types in c++11 mode. To support other scalar types, or float/double in non c++11 mode, the user has to provide implementations of betainc(\+T,\+T,\+T) for any scalar type T to be supported.
\end{DoxyNote}

template$<$typename Polynomial $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{structEigen_1_1NumTraits}{Num\+Traits}}$<$ typename\+Polynomial\+::\+Scalar $>$\+::\+Real Eigen\+::cauchy\+\_\+max\+\_\+bound (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const Polynomial \&}]{poly}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
a maximum bound for the absolute value of any root of the polynomial.
\end{DoxyReturn}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em poly} & \+: the vector of coefficients of the polynomial ordered by degrees i.\+e. poly\mbox{[}i\mbox{]} is the coefficient of degree i of the polynomial e.\+g. $ 1 + 3x^2 $ is stored as a vector $ [ 1, 0, 3 ] $.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyPrecond}{Precondition}
the leading coefficient of the input polynomial poly must be non zero 
\end{DoxyPrecond}

\Hypertarget{namespaceEigen_ad6d0ed07a6ee97fcef4fe3bce6a674d4}\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!klu\_solve@{klu\_solve}}
\index{klu\_solve@{klu\_solve}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{klu\_solve()}{klu\_solve()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespaceEigen_ad6d0ed07a6ee97fcef4fe3bce6a674d4} 
int Eigen\+::klu\+\_\+solve (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{klu\+\_\+symbolic \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{Symbolic}{, }\item[{klu\+\_\+numeric \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{Numeric}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceEigen_a62e77e0933482dafde8fe197d9a2cfde}{Index}}}]{ldim}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceEigen_a62e77e0933482dafde8fe197d9a2cfde}{Index}}}]{nrhs}{, }\item[{double}]{B}{\mbox{[}$\,$\mbox{]}, }\item[{klu\+\_\+common \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{Common}{, }\item[{double}]{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}



A sparse LU factorization and solver based on \doxylink{classEigen_1_1KLU}{KLU}. 

This class allows to solve for A.\+X = B sparse linear problems via a LU factorization using the \doxylink{classEigen_1_1KLU}{KLU} library. The sparse matrix A must be squared and full rank. The vectors or matrices X and B can be either dense or sparse.

\begin{DoxyWarning}{Warning}
The input matrix A should be in a {\bfseries{compressed}} and {\bfseries{column-\/major}} form. Otherwise an expensive copy will be made. You can call the inexpensive make\+Compressed() to get a compressed matrix. 
\end{DoxyWarning}

\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em \+\_\+\+Matrix\+Type} & the type of the sparse matrix A, it must be a Sparse\+Matrix$<$$>$\\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}
\textbackslash{}implsparsesolverconcept

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
Tutorial\+Sparse\+Solver\+Concept, class \doxylink{classEigen_1_1UmfPackLU}{Umf\+Pack\+LU}, class \doxylink{classEigen_1_1SparseLU}{Sparse\+LU} 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\Hypertarget{namespaceEigen_a9474da5ed68bbd9a6788a999330416d6}\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!KnotAveraging@{KnotAveraging}}
\index{KnotAveraging@{KnotAveraging}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{KnotAveraging()}{KnotAveraging()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespaceEigen_a9474da5ed68bbd9a6788a999330416d6} 
template$<$typename Knot\+Vector\+Type $>$ \\
void Eigen\+::\+Knot\+Averaging (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const Knot\+Vector\+Type \&}]{parameters}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceEigen_aa06499c94936a19673e53deb516a1b76}{Dense\+Index}}}]{degree}{, }\item[{Knot\+Vector\+Type \&}]{knots}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Computes knot averages. 

The knots are computed as     \begin{align*}
 u_0 & = \hdots = u_p = 0 \\
 u_{m-p} & = \hdots = u_{m} = 1 \\
 u_{j+p} & = \frac{1}{p}\sum_{i=j}^{j+p-1}\bar{u}_i \quad\quad j=1,\hdots,n-p
\end{align*} where $p$ is the degree and $m+1$ the number knots of the desired interpolating spline.


\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em parameters} & The input parameters. During interpolation one for each data point. \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em degree} & The spline degree which is used during the interpolation. \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ out}}  & {\em knots} & The output knot vector.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
Les Piegl and Wayne Tiller, The NURBS book (2nd ed.), 1997, 9.\+2.\+1 Global Curve Interpolation \doxylink{abseil-cpp_2absl_2container_2internal_2layout__test_8cc_a633ab603a49d0a046734a0f3e6de45e9}{to} Point Data 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\end{center}
\end{figure}
\Hypertarget{namespaceEigen_ae10a6f9b6ab7fb400a2526b6382c533b}\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!KnotAveragingWithDerivatives@{KnotAveragingWithDerivatives}}
\index{KnotAveragingWithDerivatives@{KnotAveragingWithDerivatives}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{KnotAveragingWithDerivatives()}{KnotAveragingWithDerivatives()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespaceEigen_ae10a6f9b6ab7fb400a2526b6382c533b} 
template$<$typename Knot\+Vector\+Type , typename Parameter\+Vector\+Type , typename Index\+Array $>$ \\
void Eigen\+::\+Knot\+Averaging\+With\+Derivatives (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const Parameter\+Vector\+Type \&}]{parameters}{, }\item[{const unsigned int}]{degree}{, }\item[{const Index\+Array \&}]{derivative\+Indices}{, }\item[{Knot\+Vector\+Type \&}]{knots}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Computes knot averages when derivative constraints are present. Note that this is a technical interpretation of the referenced article since the algorithm contained therein is incorrect as written. 


\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em parameters} & The parameters at which the interpolation B-\/\+Spline will intersect the given interpolation points. The parameters are assumed to be a non-\/decreasing sequence. \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em degree} & The degree of the interpolating B-\/\+Spline. This must be greater than zero. \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em derivative\+Indices} & The indices corresponding to parameters at which there are derivative constraints. The indices are assumed to be a non-\/decreasing sequence. \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ out}}  & {\em knots} & The calculated knot vector. These will be returned as a non-\/decreasing sequence\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
Les \doxylink{abseil-cpp_2absl_2base_2internal_2fast__type__id__test_8cc_a1ea955b94ea8dc35e689055712257459}{A}. Piegl, Khairan Rajab, Volha Smarodzinana. 2008. Curve interpolation with directional constraints for engineering design. Engineering with Computers 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\Hypertarget{namespaceEigen_a4e6cd3acfea39bcff3fa38e0de1226f5}\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!kroneckerProduct@{kroneckerProduct}}
\index{kroneckerProduct@{kroneckerProduct}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{kroneckerProduct()}{kroneckerProduct()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespaceEigen_a4e6cd3acfea39bcff3fa38e0de1226f5} 
template$<$typename \mbox{\hyperlink{abseil-cpp_2absl_2base_2internal_2fast__type__id__test_8cc_a1ea955b94ea8dc35e689055712257459}{A}} , typename B $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1KroneckerProductSparse}{Kronecker\+Product\+Sparse}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{abseil-cpp_2absl_2base_2internal_2fast__type__id__test_8cc_a1ea955b94ea8dc35e689055712257459}{A}}, B $>$ Eigen\+::kronecker\+Product (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{structEigen_1_1EigenBase}{Eigen\+Base}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{abseil-cpp_2absl_2base_2internal_2fast__type__id__test_8cc_a1ea955b94ea8dc35e689055712257459}{A}} $>$ \&}]{a}{, }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{structEigen_1_1EigenBase}{Eigen\+Base}}$<$ B $>$ \&}]{b}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Computes Kronecker tensor product of two matrices, at least one of which is sparse

\begin{DoxyWarning}{Warning}
If you want to replace a matrix by its Kronecker product with some matrix, do {\bfseries{NOT}} do this\+: 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{A\ =\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceEigen_aedd4b7cd1e324ed0769cac2701f4d050}{kroneckerProduct}}(A,B);\ \textcolor{comment}{//\ bug!!!\ caused\ by\ aliasing\ effect}}

\end{DoxyCode}
 instead, use eval() to work around this\+: 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{A\ =\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceEigen_aedd4b7cd1e324ed0769cac2701f4d050}{kroneckerProduct}}(A,B).eval();}

\end{DoxyCode}

\end{DoxyWarning}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em a} & Dense/sparse matrix a \\
\hline
{\em b} & Dense/sparse matrix b \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Kronecker tensor product of a and b, stored in a sparse matrix 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\Hypertarget{namespaceEigen_aedd4b7cd1e324ed0769cac2701f4d050}\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!kroneckerProduct@{kroneckerProduct}}
\index{kroneckerProduct@{kroneckerProduct}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{kroneckerProduct()}{kroneckerProduct()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [2/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespaceEigen_aedd4b7cd1e324ed0769cac2701f4d050} 
template$<$typename \mbox{\hyperlink{abseil-cpp_2absl_2base_2internal_2fast__type__id__test_8cc_a1ea955b94ea8dc35e689055712257459}{A}} , typename B $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1KroneckerProduct}{Kronecker\+Product}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{abseil-cpp_2absl_2base_2internal_2fast__type__id__test_8cc_a1ea955b94ea8dc35e689055712257459}{A}}, B $>$ Eigen\+::kronecker\+Product (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Matrix\+Base}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{abseil-cpp_2absl_2base_2internal_2fast__type__id__test_8cc_a1ea955b94ea8dc35e689055712257459}{A}} $>$ \&}]{a}{, }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Matrix\+Base}}$<$ B $>$ \&}]{b}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Computes Kronecker tensor product of two dense matrices

\begin{DoxyWarning}{Warning}
If you want to replace a matrix by its Kronecker product with some matrix, do {\bfseries{NOT}} do this\+: 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{A\ =\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceEigen_aedd4b7cd1e324ed0769cac2701f4d050}{kroneckerProduct}}(A,B);\ \textcolor{comment}{//\ bug!!!\ caused\ by\ aliasing\ effect}}

\end{DoxyCode}
 instead, use eval() to work around this\+: 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{A\ =\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceEigen_aedd4b7cd1e324ed0769cac2701f4d050}{kroneckerProduct}}(A,B).eval();}

\end{DoxyCode}

\end{DoxyWarning}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}

\hline
{\em b} & \doxylink{structEigen_1_1Dense}{Dense} matrix b \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Kronecker tensor product of a and b 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\Hypertarget{namespaceEigen_a2f490197e16df831683018e383e29346}\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!matrix\_sqrt\_quasi\_triangular@{matrix\_sqrt\_quasi\_triangular}}
\index{matrix\_sqrt\_quasi\_triangular@{matrix\_sqrt\_quasi\_triangular}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{matrix\_sqrt\_quasi\_triangular()}{matrix\_sqrt\_quasi\_triangular()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespaceEigen_a2f490197e16df831683018e383e29346} 
template$<$typename Matrix\+Type , typename Result\+Type $>$ \\
void Eigen\+::matrix\+\_\+sqrt\+\_\+quasi\+\_\+triangular (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const Matrix\+Type \&}]{arg}{, }\item[{Result\+Type \&}]{result}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Compute matrix square root of quasi-\/triangular matrix. 


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em Matrix\+Type} & type of {\ttfamily arg}, the argument of matrix square root, expected to be an instantiation of the \doxylink{classEigen_1_1Matrix}{Matrix} class template. \\
\hline
{\em Result\+Type} & type of {\ttfamily result}, where result is to be stored. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em arg} & argument of matrix square root. \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ out}}  & {\em result} & matrix square root of upper Hessenberg part of {\ttfamily arg}.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
This function computes the square root of the upper quasi-\/triangular matrix stored in the upper Hessenberg part of {\ttfamily arg}. Only the upper Hessenberg part of {\ttfamily result} is updated, the rest is not touched. See Matrix\+Base\+::sqrt() for details on how this computation is implemented.

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
Matrix\+Square\+Root, Matrix\+Square\+Root\+Quasi\+Triangular 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
Here is the call graph for this function\+:

\Hypertarget{namespaceEigen_ae51c91f920f6ea4a7f6f72caa1e8249f}\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!matrix\_sqrt\_triangular@{matrix\_sqrt\_triangular}}
\index{matrix\_sqrt\_triangular@{matrix\_sqrt\_triangular}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{matrix\_sqrt\_triangular()}{matrix\_sqrt\_triangular()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespaceEigen_ae51c91f920f6ea4a7f6f72caa1e8249f} 
template$<$typename Matrix\+Type , typename Result\+Type $>$ \\
void Eigen\+::matrix\+\_\+sqrt\+\_\+triangular (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const Matrix\+Type \&}]{arg}{, }\item[{Result\+Type \&}]{result}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Compute matrix square root of triangular matrix. 


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em Matrix\+Type} & type of {\ttfamily arg}, the argument of matrix square root, expected to be an instantiation of the \doxylink{classEigen_1_1Matrix}{Matrix} class template. \\
\hline
{\em Result\+Type} & type of {\ttfamily result}, where result is to be stored. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em arg} & argument of matrix square root. \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ out}}  & {\em result} & matrix square root of upper triangular part of {\ttfamily arg}.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
Only the upper triangular part (including the diagonal) of {\ttfamily result} is updated, the rest is not touched. See Matrix\+Base\+::sqrt() for details on how this computation is implemented.

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
Matrix\+Square\+Root, Matrix\+Square\+Root\+Quasi\+Triangular 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\mbox{\hyperlink{structEigen_1_1internal_1_1matrix__type__times__scalar__type}{internal\+::matrix\+\_\+type\+\_\+times\+\_\+scalar\+\_\+type}}$<$ typename\+Vectors\+Type\+::\+Scalar, Other\+Derived $>$\+::\+Type Eigen\+::operator\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Other\+Derived $>$ \&}]{other}{, }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1HouseholderSequence}{Householder\+Sequence}}$<$ Vectors\+Type, Coeffs\+Type, Side $>$ \&}]{h}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Computes the product of a matrix with a Householder sequence. 


\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em other} & Matrix being multiplied. \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em h} & Householder\+Sequence being multiplied. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Expression object representing the product.
\end{DoxyReturn}
This function computes $ MH $ where $ M $ is the matrix {\ttfamily other} and $ H $ is the Householder sequence represented by {\ttfamily h}. Here is the call graph for this function\+:

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{polygamma()}{polygamma()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespaceEigen_a006af4897c203302a60cfabcebacff7e} 
template$<$typename DerivedN , typename DerivedX $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_af2b60117c00a6e75812de43bfe7db3b1}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+STRONG\+\_\+\+INLINE}} const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1CwiseBinaryOp}{Eigen\+::\+Cwise\+Binary\+Op}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structEigen_1_1internal_1_1scalar__polygamma__op}{Eigen\+::internal\+::scalar\+\_\+polygamma\+\_\+op}}$<$ typename Derived\+X\+::\+Scalar $>$, const DerivedN, const DerivedX $>$ Eigen\+::polygamma (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase}{Eigen\+::\+Array\+Base}}$<$ DerivedN $>$ \&}]{n}{, }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase}{Eigen\+::\+Array\+Base}}$<$ DerivedX $>$ \&}]{x}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\textbackslash{}cpp11 \begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of the coefficient-\/wise polygamma({\itshape n}, {\itshape x}) to the given arrays.
\end{DoxyReturn}
It returns the {\itshape n} -\/th derivative of the digamma(psi) evaluated at {\ttfamily x}.

\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
This function supports only float and double scalar types in c++11 mode. To support other scalar types, or float/double in non c++11 mode, the user has to provide implementations of polygamma(\+T,\+T) for any scalar type T to be supported.
\end{DoxyNote}

Convenience function for constructing a Householder sequence. 

\textbackslash{} \begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
A \doxylink{classEigen_1_1HouseholderSequence}{Householder\+Sequence} constructed from the specified arguments.
\end{DoxyReturn}
This function differs from \doxylink{namespaceEigen_a4bd4b85120e014cf1125a054b02d4d92}{householder\+Sequence()} in that the template argument {\ttfamily On\+The\+Side} of the constructed \doxylink{classEigen_1_1HouseholderSequence}{Householder\+Sequence} is set to On\+The\+Right, instead of the default On\+The\+Left. \Hypertarget{namespaceEigen_afbc3648f7ef67db3d5d04454fc1257fd}\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!roots\_to\_monicPolynomial@{roots\_to\_monicPolynomial}}
\index{roots\_to\_monicPolynomial@{roots\_to\_monicPolynomial}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{roots\_to\_monicPolynomial()}{roots\_to\_monicPolynomial()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespaceEigen_afbc3648f7ef67db3d5d04454fc1257fd} 
template$<$typename Root\+Vector , typename Polynomial $>$ \\
void Eigen\+::roots\+\_\+to\+\_\+monic\+Polynomial (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const Root\+Vector \&}]{rv}{, }\item[{Polynomial \&}]{poly}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Given the roots of a polynomial compute the coefficients in the monomial basis of the monic polynomial with same roots and minimal degree. If Root\+Vector is a vector of complexes, Polynomial should also be a vector of complexes. 
\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em rv} & \+: a vector containing the roots of a polynomial. \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ out}}  & {\em poly} & \+: the vector of coefficients of the polynomial ordered by degrees i.\+e. poly\mbox{[}i\mbox{]} is the coefficient of degree i of the polynomial e.\+g. $ 3 + x^2 $ is stored as a vector $ [ 3, 0, 1 ] $. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_af2b60117c00a6e75812de43bfe7db3b1}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+STRONG\+\_\+\+INLINE}} const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1CwiseBinaryOp}{Eigen\+::\+Cwise\+Binary\+Op}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structEigen_1_1internal_1_1scalar__zeta__op}{Eigen\+::internal\+::scalar\+\_\+zeta\+\_\+op}}$<$ typename Derived\+X\+::\+Scalar $>$, const DerivedX, const DerivedQ $>$ Eigen\+::zeta (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase}{Eigen\+::\+Array\+Base}}$<$ DerivedX $>$ \&}]{x}{, }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase}{Eigen\+::\+Array\+Base}}$<$ DerivedQ $>$ \&}]{q}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of the coefficient-\/wise zeta({\itshape x}, {\itshape q}) to the given arrays.
\end{DoxyReturn}
It returns the Riemann zeta function of two arguments {\itshape x} and {\itshape q\+:} 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em x} & is the exponent, it must be \texorpdfstring{$>$}{>} 1 \\
\hline
{\em q} & is the shift, it must be \texorpdfstring{$>$}{>} 0\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
This function supports only float and double scalar types. To support other scalar types, the user has to provide implementations of zeta(\+T,\+T) for any scalar type T to be supported.
\end{DoxyNote}

\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\Hypertarget{namespaceEigen_ad81fa7195215a0ce30017dfac309f0b2}\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!Dynamic@{Dynamic}}
\index{Dynamic@{Dynamic}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Dynamic}{Dynamic}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespaceEigen_ad81fa7195215a0ce30017dfac309f0b2} 
const int Eigen\+::\+Dynamic = -\/1}

This value means that a positive quantity (e.\+g., a size) is not known at compile-\/time, and that instead the value is stored in some runtime variable.

Changing the value of Dynamic breaks the ABI, as Dynamic is often used as a template parameter for \doxylink{classEigen_1_1Matrix}{Matrix}. \Hypertarget{namespaceEigen_a73c597189a4a99127175e8167c456fff}\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!DynamicIndex@{DynamicIndex}}
\index{DynamicIndex@{DynamicIndex}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{DynamicIndex}{DynamicIndex}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespaceEigen_a73c597189a4a99127175e8167c456fff} 
const int Eigen\+::\+Dynamic\+Index = 0xffffff}

\Hypertarget{namespaceEigen_a3163430a1c13173faffde69016b48aaf}\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!HugeCost@{HugeCost}}
\index{HugeCost@{HugeCost}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{HugeCost}{HugeCost}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespaceEigen_a3163430a1c13173faffde69016b48aaf} 
const int Eigen\+::\+Huge\+Cost = 10000}

This value means that the cost to evaluate an expression coefficient is either very expensive or cannot be known at compile time.

This value has to be positive to (1) simplify cost computation, and (2) allow to distinguish between a very expensive and very very expensive expressions. It thus must also be large enough to make sure unrolling won\textquotesingle{}t happen and that sub expressions will be evaluated, but not too large to avoid overflow. \Hypertarget{namespaceEigen_a7951593b031e13d90223c83d022ce99e}\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!Infinity@{Infinity}}
\index{Infinity@{Infinity}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Infinity}{Infinity}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespaceEigen_a7951593b031e13d90223c83d022ce99e} 
const int Eigen\+::\+Infinity = -\/1}

This value means +Infinity; it is currently used only as the p parameter to \doxylink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a3312bfc4fd6b398acdadecbcedf7a1fc}{Matrix\+Base\+::lp\+Norm$<$int$>$()}. The value Infinity there means the L-\/infinity norm. \Hypertarget{namespaceEigen_ad3a7fa97adf0db7055c92f466cecc271}\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!InnerRandomAccessPattern@{InnerRandomAccessPattern}}
\index{InnerRandomAccessPattern@{InnerRandomAccessPattern}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{InnerRandomAccessPattern}{InnerRandomAccessPattern}}

Can be used as a parameter to \doxylink{namespaceEigen_a6db24b502633d158c17cb0677e7be4cb}{Eigen\+::seq} and \doxylink{namespaceEigen_a3a3c346d2a61d1e8e86e6fb4cf57fbda}{Eigen\+::seqN} functions to symbolically reference the last element/row/columns of the underlying vector or matrix once passed to \doxylink{classEigen_1_1DenseBase_a4ab85c7f3859f871bda589ee9cba93f2}{Dense\+Base\+::operator()(const Row\+Indices\&, const Col\+Indices\&)}.

This symbolic placeholder supports standard arithmetic operations.

A typical usage example would be\+: 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{keyword}{using\ namespace\ }\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceEigen}{Eigen}};}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespaceEigen_a06808a853a9baa38b23a5368e7491abd} 
const int Eigen\+::\+Undefined\+Incr = 0xfffffe}

This value means that the increment to go from one value to another in a sequence is not constant for each step.
